I oven fried my wings (seasoned them with season salt, garlic and pepper) and floured them.  I didnt use the egg, instead after I floured them I sprayed them with pam.  They came out nice and crispy, I baked them at 400.  After they were "fried" in the oven, I added the sauce and it was perfect. Great recipe and I was glad that I was able to make them healthier by oven frying them. I will definitely make them again.

These are soooo good! I had a chicken wing night in which I prepared these, the Restaurant-Style Buffalo Chicken Wings, and the Honey Lime Chicken Wings. They all were great, but these Japanese Chicken Wings were our favorite. So sweet, so flavorful, so crispy, so moist! One word of caution... line your roasting/baking pan with sturdy aluminum foil. The sugar/vinegar sauce gets very gooey near the end of the baking portion of the recipe and can be tough to clean up.

text:
I definitely suggest making this recipe without the egg, flour or frying.  I don't like to fry food unless it is really necessary to improve the taste and in this case it isn't necessary and in my opinnion does not inprove taste.  To make my chicken I used wings, cut them up and put them in a bowl.  I then poured about 1-2 teaspoons of extra virgin olive oil on them and made sure all the wings had a light coating of oil.  I then placed the wigs on a broiler pan and put them in the oven (set to broil) until the wings were brown on one side and then I browned the other side.  This is much faster than frying, uses much less oil and is much healthier.  I then put the wings in a baking dish with the sauce mixture from the recipe (I only used half a cup of sugar) and cooked them in the oven like the recipe says.  This way tasted much better than frying (in my opinion). But also, this way, the wings are less crispy.  If you want crispy wings you better fry them.

text:
Awesome!  I used only 1/2 of the sugar recipe calls for and used half white vinegar and half seasoned rice vinegar found in Asian markets.  I tried 3 different cooking variations: 1)followed the recipe's cooking method using butter to fry in before putting it in the oven. This was good, but I felt the butter overpowered the goodness of the sauce -btw, I LOVE butter, but frying the wings in butter was a step you can definitely omit and save the calories on. 2) I followed reviewers suggestions and oven-fried. I coated with egg & flour and baked @ 400 for 25 min turning once then added sauce and baked additional 30 min @ 350.  This was by far the best. The skin was nice and crispy and the sauce was fabulous. 3) I coated with egg and panko flakes, baked @400 for 25 turning once, added sauce, baked addition 30 @350. This was also good and my second favorite. the panko really soaks up the sauce and gives the wing a more sweet-sticky coat then a crispy-sticky. so it depends on your taste.  For all 3 variations, once the sauce was added (lined baking sheet with foil for easier cleanup), I turned the wings a few times and then removed the wings from the sauce and placed on fresh foil over baking sheet for the last 5 min.Can't wait to make it again! I forgot to add the sesame seeds like the pictures show and really wish I didn't. I'm sure the sesame seeds are a perfect touch..

Sorry to have to give this one a negative rating. While the finished product looked and smelled wonderful and was relatively easy to prepare, the taste was overpoweringly sweet. I should have known better, but given the high ratings, thought that all these reviewers can't be wrong. Some mentioned adding cayenne pepper to "balance the sweetness" but in retrospect, I'm rather inclined believe that there's something a little wrong with a chicken dish that has as much sugar in it as an average dessert. Perhaps I'd use it again as an appetizer where you'd only eat one or two, but as a main dish for already sugar-addicted kids I'd vote no.

text:
I give this recipe a B+. It tasted great, but required some tweaks. Here are a few tips to make excellent Japanese Chicken Wings, with less fat and MORE taste:
1. Do not fry. Waste of calories. Instead, broil on high in oven. Each side approx 4-5 minutes. Ensure you flip sides so all of wing is alittle crispy.
2. Once broiling is complete, remove wings from oven. Turn off broil function. Preheat oven to 375 degrees.
3. Line a sheet pan twice with foil. For recipes contents, forget about part with butter because we did not fry. Instead focus on sauce part. Do not use 1 cup of sugar. Use approx 1/3 of a cup. Use rice wine vinegar instead of white. For vinegar, use about 1/3 cup as well. Use about 6 TB of soya sauce or for taste you prefer. Slight sprinkle of chile peppers or hot sauce. Coat broiled wings in this mix well.
4. Once coated, please on cooking sheet and place in oven. Will cook for about 30 minutes. While wings cooking in oven, place leftover sauce in saucepan. Bring to a boil to use as a glaze. To thicken sauce, add cornstarch (to ensure no lumps in this sauce/gravy- add approx 1 TB of cornstarch to about 3TB of water, mix well and then add to saucepan to thicken sauce).
5. After approx 30 mins or until wings are cooked, remove from oven and coat them in the thickened sauce.
6. Service with white Nishiki rice or simply some veg. VERY delicious and enjoy!! :-)

text:
These wings were AMAZING, I adlibed a couple things to make them way better (in my opinion).

Changes to the sauce:

Used white wine vinagar instead of white vinagar. 
Used brown sugar instead of white sugar.
Added a touch of hoisen sauce. 
Added red pepper flakes. 
Added toasted sesame seeds. 
Added minced garlic AND garlic powder. 

Cooking method changes:

Instead of using egg and flour and frying in butter, I did what others suggested and coated them in olive oil, salt and pepper and then "oven fried" them for about 15 min  @ 500 in the oven turning 2 twice. Then added the sauce and baked them uncovered for 20 min @ 350, turning evenly. Then I put them in the broiler for about 3-5 mins per side or until crispy and sticky... drizzle with the reduced sauce and enjoy!

text:
So delicious! This recipe is really pretty easy and so flexible.  I have made the wings twice.  The first time I made them exactly as written and got such rave reviews I wasn't sure whether to try it any other way.  Thought I would give oven frying a shot to save calories and they were just as good - maybe better!  I coated them with seasoned flour (no egg, just flour, cayanne pepper, paprika, garlic powder, and salt), sprayed with olive oil, and bake 35-40 mins at 400, flipping them halfway, turn up the heat if you want them crispy).  Then I made twice the sauce and added about a teaspoon of cornstarch to help with thickening.  I threw the wings and all the sauce into a shallow baking dish and back into the oven for another 35 mins or so, turning occasionally.  So so good!  They became even stickier than the fried version and had less of a breaded texture - fantastic!  Guests loved them and they went faster than the always adored Restaurant-Style Buffalo Wings from this site!  The sauce is also delicious on chicken breasts and rice!

text:
I did the healthier version, and they were great!!
1. Broil wings on high in oven.  Broil 4-5 minutes. Flip wings, 4-5 minutes more, so all of wing is a little crispy. 
2. Remove wings from oven. Turn off broil function. Preheat oven to 375 degrees. 
3. Line a sheet pan with foil and spray w/ oil. Mix sauce ingredients in mixing bowl. Coat broiled wings w/ mixture. 
4. Once coated, place on cooking sheet and place in oven. Cook for about 30 minutes. While wings cooking in oven, place leftover sauce in saucepan. Bring to a boil to use as a glaze. 
To thicken sauce, add cornstarch (to ensure no lumps, add approx 1 TB of cornstarch to about 3TB of water, mix well and then add cornstarch to saucepan). 
5. After approx 30 mins or until wings are cooked, remove from oven and coat them in the thickened sauce. ...then I stuck them back in the oven for 5 more min just to carmelize the sauce onto the wings.

text:
Tracy, thank you for this fabulous recipe!  I deep fried our wings (about 12 mins).   Once they were done, I tossed them with the prepared sauce in a large bowl and poured them onto a foil-lined (and Pam sprayed) jelly roll pan and baked for about 20 mins, basting a few times.  I sprinkled with some toasted sesame seeds during the last few mins. of baking.  I used Splenda for the sauce and it worked perfectly.  One note with the Splenda -- I started with half a cup, based on reviews saying a full cup of sugar was a little too sweet.  It tasted great at that point.  I heated it through, though, before tossing with the wings, and it lost some of its sweetness.  Not sure if that's the Splenda or the heating process, but I did end up adding the other half cup of Splenda to get the sweetness back up.  I made a second batch of sauce to serve for dipping (just thickened by adding a little cornstarch/water mix and microwaving for a few mins).  The wings were SO scrumptious -- and they were even better reheated the next evening.  The technique and flavor are so wonderful...please try this one, folks -- you won't be disappointed (especially if you like the TGIFriday's chicken with JD Dipping Sauce!). Thank you again...we LOVE this recipe! :)

text:
I've modified this recipe a bit, since I'm not much good at frying (although I do love fried food).  I saute an onion with some garlic until they're nice and brown, then add some chicken legs to the pan.  I cook the legs just until theyre starting to brown, then add a little liquid (chicken stock usually, though water works in a pinch), cover, and cook on about medium heat until the legs are nearly done.  Then I uncover the pan, add the sauce ingredients (leaving out the garlic, since there's already some in the pan, and cutting back on the sugar), and simmer until the sauce thickens and the legs are done (only a few minutes).  Stir in some garlic-chili sauce for heat (or add red pepper flakes when you add sauce ingredients), and serve over some good rice (I like basmati, but use whatever you have around).  A little green onion and cilantro on top helps too.  Easy and delicious, and less of an ordeal than frying.  Definitely a good base to play around with though.

text:
These wings kick butt and will impress everyone!  The sugar that's called for is necessary to create a sticky, carmelized sauce. These are sweet, but I have 2 suggestions to counter that sweetness so it's not too much. First, I put some chile sesame oil in with the butter to add a little heat to it. Fresh chiles would probably work well in the sauce, too. Second, serve these with Japanese sticky rice.  Use a short grain rice or use jasmine or basmati. The sticky rice is bland enough to contrast nicely with the yummy sauce, which is wonderfully gooey and flavorful. Make sure you baste these. About half-way through you can start basting with the juices that are falling off the wings and carmelizing. I used fresh garlic and mixed in a little pineapple juice into the sauce instead of water and I added chopped green onion--also a nice garnish. I think this method would work great on chicken breasts, as well, since there is more meat on them to absorb the sweet sauce. I've never made wings before and I'm just so pleased with these. They were so easy. One last thing--wash that pan right away or you'll be sorry later.

If you aren't sure about making these, cut the recipe in half to just try it, which is what I did. Now I can't wait to serve these at a party. Thanks for this gem!

I really enjoyed this recipe! However... I did cut out the butter and didn't fry them. Next time I will only use 1/4 cup of sugar. I really don't think they need to be fried either, cut out the butter and save yourself the calories! Oven fry instead!

text:
Terrific! I tweaked a lil (mostly b/c I'm lazy).  The only change I made to the sauce was to use fresh garlic instead of garlic powder. I made a half batch (just 2 of us) but wish I'd made a full batch.  I fried in oil (as I was already going to fry a few other items) and I didn't dredge in egg and flour.  I just fried them plain in the oil for about 10 minutes to get them partially cooked and the skin starting to crisp.  Then placed them in a baking pan (lined with foil) and poured the sauce over them.  I moved them around and flipped them a couple times, spooning the sauce over them.  At first the sauce seems watery but at about the 45 minute mark it got all sticky and bubbly.  I cannot wait to make these again.

This is a keeper!

text:
Oh boy, I've been re-invited to the next party! I'm one of those that tries a recipe as written the first time. Usually. I did change things very slightly here. I eliminated the egg and cut the sugar to 3/4 cup. I floured the wings in a plastic freezer bag. Refrigerate the floured wings for 45 minutes. I did everything else according to the recipe. *IMPORTANT* Baste every 6-8 minutes. Now the new. Duplicate, in a sauce pan, the exact sauce recipe that you just used on the wings. Add 2 teaspoons of cornstarch to 2 teaspoons of COLD water. Then add as much cayenne pepper as you like. The sauce will thicken perfectly. If it becomes too thick, just add a couple of tablespoons of water. The original recipe will please everyone, but you can make this as hot as you like with the dip. Enjoy!

text:
WoW! These wings are delicious!  I love chicken and found this recipe to be a great way to diversify this main staple. I basically followed the recipe exactly (frying in sweet cream salted butter was a first, but definitely not the last, smelled great) except that I wanted my wings hot so I soaked them (for a few minutes)in an egg/redhot mixture before coating them in flour. Then let them sit in the fridge for about a half hour (as suggested by another 'chef'), I then coated them one last time in the flour mixture (flour and cayenne pepper)right before frying. In addtion, I put the pan under the broiler for about 5 minutes as they weren't 'crispy' enough for my taste. I added green onions and sesame seeds as toppers. These were addictive and can't wait to make again!

text:
These turned out really well, but my Japanese-Canadian bf asked whats Japanese about this recipe?  Not too much, but these were good nonetheless.  I did a couple of changes to the recipe.  To make it a bit more Asian I substituted  cup of the white vinegar for rice wine vinegar.  I also added about a tablespoon of sesame oil.  I only used  a cup of sugar, but next time I would only add  a cup, as it was a tiny bit sweet for my taste.  I used low sodium soy sauce and completely left out the salt.  As for the cooking time, I listened to other reviewers and decided to bake them instead of frying.  I coated them in flour and sprayed them with Pam.  I baked them for about 45 minutes at 425, turning them over every 15 minutes.  I then set it to high heat broil, and added the sauce.  I broiled them for about 12 minutes, turning them over and basting the wings every 4 minutes.  Not exactly Japanese, but its a great Asian inspired recipe!

OMG! This was SO tasty!  I followed the advice of others and did not egg and fry the chicken.  Instead I layed the pieces in a single layer in a roasting pan, sprinkled a little olive oil, then flour, salt, pepper, and garlic powder and cooked the chicken about 15 minutes on 400F.  I made one other yummy adustment to the sauce - I added a heaping scoop of creamy peanut butter, stirred well, and poured over the chicken.  Frequent basting, about every 10 mins, is important.  Also, as others have suggested - line your pan with heavy foil, thje sauce will be very gooey. YUMM!

These were wonderfully sweet and gooey.  I had about 4 1/2 pounds of wings so I doubled the sauce.  I pre-seasoned the wings with salt, pepper, garlic and onion powder, dipped in egg and flour and browned them in a cast iron skillet with 1/2 Crisco and 1/2 butter.  I used raw apple cider vinegar, less sugar and I added some ginger.  Next time I will simmer the sauce first and add some cornstarch to thicken it.  It took lots longer then 30 minutes for the sauce to thicken on the wings.  I tossed some toasted sesame seeds on top when they were done.  Great Superbowl appetizer!

text:
My husband *really* enjoyed this dish. 
I made some changes- strips of boneless skinless chicken breast, 1/2 C sugar instead of 1 C, lightly frying in canola oil vs butter. Generally the same amount of sweet is used to balance the sugar, so I stuck with that ratio, 1/2C sugar to 1/2 C vinegar.
I wish the sauce had thickened instead of remaining thin, but possibly if I had used the 1C of sugar it would have. I tried boiling it on the stove before spooning it over the chicken, but that didn't help. Next time I'll probably add 2tsp cornstarch to the sauce to thicken it. 
This is a very good recipe that allows changes to suit the chef. :)

text:
Excellent.  Although I modified this recipe (not by much) it was wonderful and deserves 5 stars.  To make it healthier, I did the following:  Placed wings in a single layer in foil pan, seasoned to taste on one side (McCormick Garlic & Herb, Onion Powder, Garlic Powder, Paprika).  Placed 1 Tbs. Parkay in each corner of the pan and baked slightly covered for 45 minutes at 350 degrees.  I then turned chicken and seasoned again - recovered and baked an additional 25 minutes.  I made the sauce as stated except I used 3/4 cups sugar.  After the 25 minutes in the oven, I poured sauce over chicken and baked an additional 10 minutes uncovered.  They were very delicious.

text:
Not bad, I made this a few times until it was just right.  As is, here are a couple gotchas.  If you use egg and flour in the skillet with the cup of butter, make sure butter is hot!!!!! otherwise the wings will clump and make scrambled egg and flour mess in the pot.  Your almost better off using deep-fryer for  a couple minutes for browning.  I have read others mention to broil instead of fry, I will try that next time too.  Another item which we preferred was pick up some rice flour ( maybe a buck for 3 pounds )  instead of all-purpose flour.  it is much lighter and adheres better to the wings unless you have a few hours to chill in fridge before browning.   Now for the sauce.  add a shot of amaretto and some ground ginger to the soy and vinegar combo.  gives it that much needed asian flavor boost. other than that, this is pretty easy and good.  no blue-cheese needed.  Oh and it will work fine with a cup of splenda instead of sugar.   a cup of sugar in a wing recipe is a bit excessive.  I can see a cup in a cheesecake recipe but not for an appetizer.  the butter alone will do enough damage.

This chicken is amazing! I cut the sugar in half, mixed in a dash of cayenne with the flour,and added some chopped onion to the sauce right before baking. It turned out fantastic! I served it as a main dish along with some vegetable fried rice.

I took a short cut and didn't dredge the wings and fry them first.  I marinated the wings first for 4 hours in a simple soy sauce and ginger mixture.  Then draied the wings and placed them in a FOIL lined pan.  Baked at 450 for 20 minutes then began basting with sauce every 15 minutes or so until nice and brown.  I can see why you would want to dredge and fry first.  The sauce "sticks" better.  But these still were very good and the company loved them.

Very Good!!  I made it w/chicken breasts & the hubby loved it & has asked if it can be a "regular" weekly meal (he doesn't normally like chicken). 

I did make a couple of changes.  I cut out the butter (didn't see a need for it), doubled the soy sauce & water, cut the sugar down to 1/2-3/4 C. (otherwise too sweet), cut the vinegar to 1/4-1/2 C., used minced garlic (hate the powdered stuff) & added 1/2 t. mustard powder.  I turned the chicken breasts a few times during baking to make sure they were coated with the sauce, served over rice & sprinkled cashews on top.

text:
These wings are out of this world! Made them for a football party and everyone raved and asked that I make them for every future party LOL. 

I oven fried them for about 30 minutes at 350 and then broiled them on high on each side for a few minutes to really crisp them up. I double the sauce to make sure they were really moistened, so I wouldn't have to keep basting them. When they were finished, there was a lot of the sauce remaining in the pan so I feared they would be dripping wet, but it seems the sugar really "latched" onto the wings. The meat fell right off the bone and the skin was extremely flavorful. Can't wait to make them again!

text:
I followed a reviewer and did not fry these before baking them. Afterwards I read that frying first will help keep the coating on them, and prevent them from sticking. I baked mine at 400 for 25 minutes (after coating them in egg & flour) then I put the sauce on and baked them at 350 for the rest of the time. The result was a burnt & smoky mess. My wings stuck so badly to the pan even though I had sprayed PAM and the sauce was burned. My husband still ate them (God bless him!) and through the burnt sauce I could tell that had I not burned them they would have been great! I had to throw away my pan! I would like to try these again and fry them first.

text:
These wings are definitely good.  Also, I like to add a couple cloves of garlic, some red chili flakes, and a pinch of cayenne pepper. Don't skip crisping the wings before adding the sauce.  It makes the wings sticky, crispy, and perfect. I pour out the juice from the wings after I crisp them to avoid watering down the sauce.  It's a small step that makes a difference.  I guarantee you'll love these wings.

text:
Very good wings!  I made some for our Super Bowl "Pre Game" meal  aka lunch.   I took the advice from other reviewers;  instead of frying the wings I baked them.  Marinated wings with salt & pepper the night before.  This morning, I dusted the wings with min. amount of flour, sprayed with PAM then baked at 400F for 40 minutes, turned once.    Cooked the sauce in a sauce pan, using the ingredients suggested plus 1 tablespoon of cornstarch, until thickened.  Used a pastry brush to apply the sauce on both sides of wings.  Baked at 400F and basted every 8 - 10 minutes for a total of 35 minutes.  Just had enough sauce for that purpose.  The wings were sticky but not messy.  My husband and our son loved them.    Thanks for the recipe!  Definitely will make them again.

text:
My family thoroughly enjoyed them. I changed it a bit: I did not fry, but oil, season (salt, pepper, dry mustard, garlic powder)and egg white (mix up the chicken in a bowl to coat and season)lightly flour and bake in oven for about 20 mins to brown and broil for last 15-20 mins (or however you desire for crispiness and brownness). Once crispy, baste w/ sauce until chicken is done. For sauce, double it. Use half of sugar. Last batch of sauce when basting, add a little cornstarch/water mix to thicken.

While browsing recipes for chicken wings, I couldn't help but notice how many good reviews this one had. When I saw how simple the ingredients were, I had to try it. I have to say that I love the sticky, gooey sauce, and the chicken cooked perfectly.

These were delicious...I didn't dredge them in flour or fry them though for health reasons. city:
None
region:
None
country:
None
text:
These wings are showstoppers! Absolutely delicious and worth the effort to prepare them. I followed the suggestion of other testers to add cayenne to balance the sweetness, and they had a pleasant, but not overwhelming, kick. The frying in butter step was kind of scary to me until I did it - I just used the pot I normally boil pasta in, and it was deep enough to absorb all the splatters and my kitchen was not at all trashed. Per the suggestion of another tester, I did add some canola oil to the butter (about a 3:1 butter to canola ratio) and it helped the butter to not overbrown (provided you fry at med. high heat and not high). Finally, do line your roasting pan with foil to help cleanup. As these finish up in the oven, the sauce that was beautifully caramel-y and baste-able turns into a rock hard, baked-on substance (at least you'll know they're done)! Also, I prepped these through the frying stage the night before, then refrigerated. Save a few extra minutes in the oven, they turned out just as lovely.

text:
Very tasty chicken dish.  After reading the reviews I made some simple changes to add more flavor and thicken the sauce. 1) I used 2 pounds boneless, skinless chicken thighs.  2) Marinated the chicken in the sauce all day.  3) Removed chicken from sauce and fried according to the directions.  4) Strained the sauce into a small saucepan and added 1 T. of cornstarch and heated until thickened, then poured over the chicken to bake.  This came out very flavorful, sweet and sticky!

8 13 17 ... http://allrecipes.com/recipe/23312/japanese-chicken-wings/ ... 'Made this & these ... http://allrecipes.com/recipe/88438/teriyaki-chicken-wings/ ... While neither was "the bomb," K liked these, Japanese, better. I fry when necessary so didn't. :D To one cup flour, added 1/2t ea paprika & garlic powder. Cayenne would be a good addition to the flour & omitting water or subbing for more soy sounds like it'd be better, too. I floured 'em & baked on a moderately-oiled foil-lined sheet; placed More-skin-side down in oil then turned over n sprayed em with oil on the floury parts. Baked at 400, thirty minutes; turned over the drumettes & baked thirty more. 'Sauced everyone till lookin' good, 20? The flavor of these is predominantly sweet, slightly sweet; no soy or tang from the vinegar detectable. This baking method - first time I've tried - was good. Yay for me! :) Thanks for the recipe, TLTRN!

text:
These were really good!  I followed the recipe exactly with one exception, I fried the wings in a mix of peanut and olive oil instead of butter.  Worked fine.  I also used wing sections (about 26-28).  Be careful not to place your pan too low in the oven or you'll burn the sugar in the sauce and that's a difficult mess to clean up.  Unless you're using a good quality non-stick pan, line it with heavy duty aluminum foil.  I turned mine once, half way through the baking time, which sufficed for basting.  You can really smell the vinegar while these are in the oven, but don't worry, the end result is sweet and delicious.  Mine were done in 35 mins.  Will definitely make these again.

text:
I know that people are changing this recipe to make a healthier version, but this version is perfect just the way it is. We make these wings once a year, because they are so fattening, but it is a very special treat. We do not tweak the recipe at all. I made these for my boyfriend the first time he came over to dinner. He is still with me 8 years later, and still talks about these wings as his favorite dish. I maintain that this is the reason he stays with me. HA! These wings are the ONLY food I eat fried. I have tried the other recipe suggestions, and so far, this exact recipe is the best and most well received. If you have dietary restrictions, go ahead and switch it up. However, if you want a decadent, sinfully unhealthy treat once in a while, definitely try these. They are easy to make, extremely messy, and a hit with everyone who has ever tasted them.

text:
I read another review and decided to bake instead of fry - well, sort of.  I put a few pats of butter and several large spoonfuls of coconut oil into a broiler pan (foil lined) and then placed the flour dredged wings (didn't use egg, the flour stuck just fine)side by side in it.  I cooked in a 400 degree oven, 20 minutes on each side, but I did kick it up to 450 in the last 5 minutes (only one drumette was overcooked, the rest of the wings and drumettes were perfect).  I also doubled the sauce (using my own homemade garlic/soy sauce) because there never seems to be enough and I'm glad I did.  I poured half over them and the other half when I flipped, making sure to stir thoroughly.  WOW!  This was like candied, garlic chicken wings!!!  Amazingly good and sticky!  YUM!  Definitely a keeper and SO EASY!  Oh, we ate them with a little ranch dressing, uberlicious!  Thank you for the recipe!!!

I have had this recipe in my box for some time.  The sauce was good (added some fresh grated ginger and some cayenne), although sweet with 1 cup of sugar. text:
Finally something my VERY picky 10 year old will eat!!  I changed this just a bit out of necessity and screw-ups... but it still worked.  I was planning on oven-frying, but realized I just didn't have the time.  I had already floured the wings (with garlic powder, seasoned salt and pepper added in), but had NOT egged them.  I decided to pan-fry just to save a little time, and I used a mixture of butter and canola oil.  Because I hadn't egged first, I probably lost most of the flour coating, but it still turned out well.  I cut down on the sugar in the sauce just a bit (about 3/4 cup instead), and didn't put in quite as much salt as called for (soy sauce is salty enough).  I baked them at about 400 degrees for about half an hour, basting 3 or 4 times.  My daughter called them her "favorite meal ever!"

This is the best wing recipe ever with the following changes: I used chicken strips instead of wings and fried them (for a total of 10 minutes, turning over after 5 min.) in a half stick of butter and a half cup of olive oil (this prevents the butter from burning). text:
First...this was very tasty like sweet and sour chicken.  I made a few changes:
1) I did use egg (brown cage free healthy) and whole wheat flour that I seasoned and browned both sides of the chicken in olive oil...not butter.  
2) I had leg and thighs but this still worked well.
3) I made the sauce the day before and the flavor was more uniformed.  
4) I used the extra sauce that I had from the pan that the chicken was cooking in the oven in some whole wheat noodles that I had to go with this dish.

If you are going to reduce the sugar by say 1/2 cup then change the amount of the other ingredients as well but make the sauce ahead so that the flavors have a chance to blend.  

This was great and I can't wait to make it again!

text:
These were an absolute delight. I, like many others, "oven fried" the wings which turned out really well but while preparing the sauce it seemed as if the vinegar overwhelmed the spices even while checkin on them in the oven it was still dominant however once the wings were complete the sauce had caramelized and thickened and the harsh vinegar smell was leveled out by the sugar. I was tremendously leary on how well they would turn out but I am extremely happy that I took the chance. I believe if u use less sugar you will be overwhelmed by the vinegary smell and taste. I used 3/4 cup of sugar but followed the original recipe to a tee aside from "oven frying." It was really simplistic and cut down on my cooking time. If you choose to "oven fry" take your wings and season them as you normally would deep frying. Once floured, place in a baking dish which has been coated with non stick cooking spray. Set oven to 450 and bake for abt 40 minutes.* Pour sauce onto the wings and then place back into the oven for about 20 additional minutes. Make sure to turn your chicken half thru both baking times. Enjoy!

text:
Wow! Can I give it 10 stars for taste? I added Lowry's Seasoning salt and garlic pepper to the flour, and fried the wings in "I can't believe its not butter". I decreased the sugar in the sauce by 1/3 and added about 2 tsp of sesame oil. I baked them for an hour, basting every 10 minutes and turning them once. For the last 10 minutes, I cranked the heat up to 400 so that they would crisp up. When they were done, I sprinkled them with toasted sesame seeds. They tasted fantastic, just like what a wing place night have, or an entree on an Asian buffet. My reason for giving this only 4 stars is because the coating did not stay on very well. It was already coming off by the second time I basted the wings. Not that it's that big of a deal because the wings were very tender and absorbed the sauce well, but I think I will double flour the wings next time. Can't wait to make again! Thanks for a great recipe!

all i can see is OMG. These are incredible. Even my picky 5 year old gobbled these up and asked for more. Here are the only changes I made to them.
I beat the egg and put the wings in the egg.  I added plenty of flour to coat them and fried them in about 1/3 cup of butter. Just enough to get them brown and not dry out as I fried them.  I made the sauce with 1/2 c. brown sugar and 1/2 c. white sugar.  I added a a tsp of ground ginger and used ginger flavord soy sauce and added chopped green onions and seasme seeds to the sauce and boiled it to melt the sugar. Pour the sauce over the wings and basted every 10-15 mins. Baked about 55 min and these were PERFECT. I will be making these over and over again!!!!!!!

I read the first three pages of this recipe's reviews. I decided not to fry them - I dipped the wings (frozen) in flour, sprayed them with Pam and then cooked them on 375 for 35 minutes - turned them and cooked for 25 minutes more. I then basted them with the sauce - which I made more of (12 pounds of chicken wings to be exact) and used half of the called for amount.  They cooked for another 20 minutes - half way thru I had my hubby baste them again.  I then broiled them for an additional 5 minutes. I do not eat chicken on the bone but my hubby and the people I served these to loved them. My hubby said that the wings I bought were a little fatty (my fault) but overall they tasted amazing! I will make again!

text:
This is soooooo good. I have tried it both with breading and frying the wings and baking them "naked". I would say I prefer the wings "naked" and it is less time consuming that way. However, I also make this recipe with pounded skinless, boneless chicken breast and I do dredge and fry those and serve over rice with extra sauce. I do reduce the white sugar just a skitch. I never pour all the sauce over the top when baking. I make twice the marinade pour only 1/4 over the top, then I boil the marinade on the stovetop to thicken and then baste often with the syrup. The chicken turns out sticky and incredible. I am not usually a chicken fan but this is my favorite way to prepare it. I also omit the sesame seeds because my husband doesn't like them. Thanks.

This was my first attempt at making wings. I was surprised how tasty they were. I had to scale the recipe because I had 4 1/2 lbs. of wings. I took these wings to a potluck with 30 people and they were a big hit! I made two big pans of them and they were gone in no time. I would highly recommend this recipe to anyone. I have an 18 month old baby and I can only do things while he is sleeping. So while he was down for a nap I breaded and fried the whole batch and put them in the fridge. The next day I layed them out on two big pans and I tripled the sauce recipe and poured it over the wings. There was extra sauce but I still poured the rest over the wings and by the time I got to the party they were still warm and the sauce had thickened which made them extra tasty and sticky! Isn't that what makes a good wing! We like our wings saucey. Just do what works for you. Thanks Tracy for our new favorite wing recipe!

I made these with legs since my market didn't have any wings, and I also used a veg/sesame oil mix to fry the legs in rather than the butter and thickened the sauce with some cornstarch. I may try these again with breasts or wings and see if we like them better with white meat.  This is a good occaisional dish since it has so much sugar, but it was nice to do something different with chicken.  Thanks!

I always change recipes...always. Largely because I read the reviews first. I was lazy about using the egg. I always have a flour mix on hand that I use regularly  (1/2 c flour, 1/4 tsp ea of paprika, cayenne, & salt). I used that on 7 large wings, halved. I used 1/2 a stick of butter and veg.oil. I used 1/2 c sugar & 1/3 c of vinegar. The rest remained unchanged. I lined a glass pan with foil & flipped the wings about 4 times during the 45 minute bake time. I think I fried my wings about 15 minutes. They didn't come out crispy how I did it, but my husband LOVED them.

This was great!!  I made it and took the advice of a few people who made some changes.  I am sure cooking the wings in butter will make it taste great, but I wanted to cut out some of the fat so I baked mine in the oven with just the flour coating and a spray of veggie oil. I  I also used brown sugar instead of white and they tasted fantastic.  Make sure you pat dry the wings before coating with flour.  (if you have some patience, try and pull some of the skin off of the wings to cut out even more fat. ) Will make again soon!!!!

text:
Quite delicious wings. Takes some effort but very easy to make.
However, this recipe is too sweet for me. I think kids might like it this way, but I would prefer it way less sweeter.

Here are some things I would change next time.

1. Use 1/2 cup of sugar
2. 2 tablespoons of water
3. 1 tablespoon of garlic power in the flour
4. 1 tablespoon of fine black pepper in the flour.

The wings were way better with "Pure Louisiana Crystal Extra Hot" hot sauce.

text:
I made these for a party and everyone loved them. I like to do as much in advance as possible when I entertain. The morning of the party I prepared them as directed except after dipping in egg and the flour mixture I placed the chicken wings on cookie racks sprayed with Pam and placed them in the fridge on trays. I also use this method with buffalo wings, the breading stays  on the chicken better when it  sits for a few hours. I also prepared the sauce in advance and put it in the fridge. An hour before my guests were to arrive I fried the wings, placed them in the roasting pan, poured the sauce over and put them in the oven.

text:
When trying this for the first time I knew one of my guests was not a fan of buffalo and super sweet wing sauce.  I halved the sugar while keeping the other ingredients the same.  I also simmered the sauce for about 30 min instead of baking it with them.  Baking the wings naked at 300 for 2 hours and broiling them at the end allowed the fat under the skin to cook away with a nice crispy exterior.  Tossed the wings in with the sauce and voila.  Within 20 min all of them were eaten and half of the wings I did buffalo style hadn't been touched.  Thankfully my friend got her share and loved it.  Great Recipe!!!!
One last thing... I sprinkled some sesame seeds over the finished product.  Didn't alter the taste too much but it did make them much more presentable.

text:
We loved these but like others, I made some changes to the recipe. I used the sauce ingredients exactly as listed except I cut the sugar in half. I skipped the frying step. I sprinkled the wings with garlic powder then roasted at 375 for 25 mins skin side up, then turned over and roasted 25 mins more.  I poured sauce over wings, roasted 15 minutes then turned and roasted 15 minutes more. I then transfered the wings to a rimmed, foil covered baking sheet and poured about 1/3 of sauce over the wings. I broiled for 3 minutes then turned and broiled for 2 more minutes. I was searching for a crispy skin and thickened sauce but it never happened. Even without the crispiness, both my husband and I thought these wings were really yummy. Will make again, for sure.UPDATE: I made these again but used 3/4 c. sugar. The sauce did caramelize under the broiler pretty quickly so I cut the broiling time to 2 mins per side. The wings still were not crispy but they were very yummy.

These were good but not worth the effort of making the wings from scratch. Anyways, I enjoyed this but not enough to make them again.

text:
This recipe was a hit with my family. Like others, I made a few tweaks (hence the 4 star rating). I opted to fry the wings as directed, but used canola oil instead of butter. I also seasoned the wings and dredged them in flour (omitting the egg). 

For the glaze, I used rice vinegar and halved the sugar . I also added grated fresh ginger and freshly minced garlic. The sauce was amazing!
I placed the wings on a rack in the oven to avoid the soggy bottom and basted them with the sauce (turning them over half way and basted the other side). Since the sauce was a bit thin, I whisked in some corn starch mixed with water to thicken it. I used the thicker sauce and gave the wings one final basting under the broiler to make them a bit stickier. It was delicious!! We used the extra sauce for dipping and on some salmon the next day.

text:
Followed other user advice and dredged the wings in flour, salt, and pepper, then sprayed with Pam and baked on a broiler pan at 400 for 20 minutes on each side.  I would recommend using aluminum foil underneath for easy cleanup.  I replaced the sugar with 1/3 - 1/2 C. Honey and added 1/2 tsp each of cayenne pepper and red pepper flakes to add some spice.  Then dipped the wings in the sauce and broiled for 5-10 minutes on each side.  Meanwhile, heated the remaining sauce and added a little corn starch mixed with water to thicken. Once the wings were done, I tossed in the remaining sauce and they were delicious.  Next time I'll try without the flour to make them a little healthier-- they didn't seem to need the breading.  Would also consider sprinkling with sesame seeds and/or shallots.  Definitely keeping this recipe!

text:
This recipe is great exactly how it's written. I've made this dozens of times over the years. The chicken wings are meant to be fried in butter. It gives the savouriness. They are not supposed to be oven baked. Chicken wings are mostly fat and are not health food. The frying with egg and flour gives them the outside sticky gooey texture they are supposed to have. They are not supposed to be crispy like a hot wing tossed in sauce. They are also supposed to be sweet. Don't cut down the sugar. This is in all likelihood anything like an authentic Japanese dish. It's kind of like Western Chinese food. Developed in the Americas to be what it is. Anyone wanting to make so many changes to the recipe should probably write there own. Try this as it is written. Most won't be disappointed.

text:
The sauce was good! I made it exactly like the recipe. While it wasn't thick, it was still very sticky and yummy. Because of all of the mixed reviews, I made it 2 ways. I made a pan just as the recipe says and a pan as suggested by some to fry it in the oven. My preference after tasting both, was baked/fried in the oven. I love love love fried foods but as it is in the recipe, the chicken did taste too much like butter (I only used 1 stick) and the breading was actually soggy once it was done. Looked crunchy but the skin fell right off the chicken and was too soft. After 1 piece I was turned off.  Now for the oven fried version, I omitted the egg as suggested. I baked at 400 for 40 minutes , flipping it half way at 20 minutes. I then poured the same sauce on it and put it back in the oven for an additional 30 minutes at 350. These wings were much better and a lot less soggy. I will make them again, all fried in the oven without the egg. The sauce as is was great! It's not a thick bbq sauce, it's more of a loose sticky sauce. All of the chicken was baked uncovered.

text:
I've now made these wings a few times and each time they come out amazing! I've taken the advice of other reviewers and I do not fry mine, I bake them. First I sprinkle seasoning salt, garlic powder and pepper on both sides, then shake them in flour and spray Pam on them. I set them in the oven at 400 for 30 mins, then pour the sauce over and put them back in and baste every ten mins for another 30. I then take the left over sauce from the baking dishes and thicken it in a saucepan with some cornstarch. When it's thickened to my preference I toss the wings in the sauce and serve! They turn out sooo saucy and delicious! Everyone loves them!

This is a great recipe, made it this sunday for football wirh the neighbors and used chicken legs.  instead of pan frying, I oven fried by rubbing them in olive oil and then floured them 20min on 400 and then flipped them for another 20min to get both sides crispy.  Then moved them to a 9x13 glass pan and added the sauce and turned the heat down to 350 and baked them for another 45min.  Then turned up to 425 for 7min.  Best chicken with this asian style that i have ever had!

Amazing.  The only change I made was I skipped dipping the wings in egg and just rolled them in flour. This was not near as messy and they were still very crispy.  I kept the wings warm in a crock pot on warm.  I took 6 pounds of these wings to a party and they were gone in the first 1/2 hour.  This was a party of about 20 with lots of other food! This is now my go to wing recipe.  NOTE:  It takes about 20 min to fry the wings and then another 30 - 45 minutes in the oven.

text:
3 stars- exactly as the recipe is. I do not like the way it turned out without the few tweaks that I used. First off- put seasonings in the flour, it adds more flavor. Make sure you don't beat the egg too much, as when I fried it the crumbs fell off. I used the butter to fry and it just became soggy and fell apart. Instead, I added butter fried it, then added oil half way up the wings and fried on both sides. I then placed in the casserole dish and added the sauce. I tripled the sauce, and tried the double broil method but it did not stick or goop. Instead I took the wings out after 10 minutes, fried them, and then heated the sauce up and used it as a dipping sauce. It was good after these changes.

text:
I really enjoyed these wings and my boyfriend did too! My only complaint is that you can get a nice crisping on the top layer but the bottom layer is soggy. We happen to prefer our wings crisp so once the wings had cooked the full cooking time I removed them from the sauce and lightly dabbed the bottom of the wings on paper towels to absorb some moisture and put them on a cookie sheet on parchment and baked them on high 475 degrees for a few minutes and then I turned the broiler on to crisp the top. Doing this achieved the texture we prefer, no knock on the recipe itself.

This is really yummy. I follow directions as is, but after frying, I cover, put in the oven for about 30 minutes. I then take it out, pour a lot of the sauce over the chicken, I then cover for another 10 minutes. I then uncover, bake for another 30 minutes, checking on it. These always go great for chinese theme night in my home, where I make egg fried rice, and a side of egg drop soup =)

text:
My friends and I loved these wings. The first time I made them I used wings, used the flour, skipped the egg. For the sauce, I cut the sugar in half, and added some ginger, crushed red pepper and some chili powder. I wanted them to be sweet and spicy. Then I sprayed the wings with butter cooking spray then baked in the oven at 375 for 35 min. turned them over and baked another 25 min. Basted with the sauce for another 20 minutes and let sit for a bit. They were very sticky and delicious. The next time I used skinless boneless chicken breasts I cut up, coated in flour, then browned at high heat. I then added sauce and cooked in oven for 30 min, basting every 8 in or so. They were great this way too.

None
text:
It was really really good, but I would suggest making it with something else besides chicken wings, like bonelss chicken leg meat or breasts.
I added 1 tbsp of cornstarch to help thicken the sauce, which at first didn't seem like it would thicken at all while it was in the oven, but I found that if you let it sit about 5-10 minutes before serving and then take some of the sauce from the bottom of the pan and pour it ontop of the chicken, that the sauce will thicken.
I also added salt and pepper to the flour and didn't add the extra salt to the sauce.  I also only put about 1/2 cup of sugar to the sauce mixture.
Finally, I added a couple chopped green onions as a garnish on top of the chicken when serving, the green onions seem to go well with the flavor of the sauce.

Wow!!! I made these for my husband and he LOVED them! I have a sweet tooth so I thought I would really love the recipe. I did, but after a while I found it a bit too sweet for me.
